data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryanair_HQ.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Ryanair Headquarters in Dublin Airport</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryanair_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ryanair_logo.svg/220px-Ryanair_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="38" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ryanair_logo.svg/330px-Ryanair_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ryanair_logo.svg/440px-Ryanair_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="430" data-file-height="74" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryanair_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ryanair\'s old logo, used from 2001 to 2013</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryanair_logo_2013(1).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/60/Ryanair_logo_2013%281%29.svg/220px-Ryanair_logo_2013%281%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="37" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/60/Ryanair_logo_2013%281%29.svg/330px-Ryanair_logo_2013%281%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/60/Ryanair_logo_2013%281%29.svg/440px-Ryanair_logo_2013%281%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="289" data-file-height="48" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryanair_logo_2013(1).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ryanair\'s previous logo used from November 2013 to July 2015, when a new logo with a white background was introduced. This logo was first revealed in January 2010.</div></div></div>\n<p>The head office of Ryanair has been in the Airside Business Park in <a href="/wiki/Swords,_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Swords, Ireland">Swords</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Dublin" title="County Dublin">County Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> since 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> David Daly, a developer, had built the facility prior to Ryanair\'s 2012 purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-Mulliganstaffmove_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mulliganstaffmove-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The building has 100,000 square feet (9,300&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space,<sup id="cite_ref-IrishBizPost_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishBizPost-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and the airline paid \xe2\x82\xac11 million to occupy the building. According to John Mulligan of the <i><a href="/wiki/Irish_Independent" title="Irish Independent">Irish Independent</a></i>, it was thought that Ryanair would refurbish the building for another \xe2\x82\xac9 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Mulliganstaffmove_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mulliganstaffmove-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previously, since 2004, the head office had been on the property of <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a>, in proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a> head office.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Darley Investments built the facility in 1992. Ryanair later purchased Darley and had a 30-year lease of the head office facility from the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Transport_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Transport of Ireland">Department of Transport of Ireland</a>. For twelve years, the company paid no rent even though it was supposed to pay \xe2\x82\xac244,000 per year. After twelve years and prior to 2008, it paid less than half of the \xe2\x82\xac244,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Mulliganstaffmove_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mulliganstaffmove-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment_relations">Employment relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Employment relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Refusal_to_recognise_unions">Refusal to recognise unions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Refusal to recognise unions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the early years, when Ryanair had a total of 450 employees who each had shares in the company, there was an agreement that staff would not join a <a href="/wiki/Labor_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor union">labor union</a> on the basis that they would have an influence on how the company was run.<sup id="cite_ref-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The treatment of employees has changed considerably since then and new employees no longer get shares in the company. Whilst Ryanair announced in December 2017 that it would recognise pilots\' unions, the company still refuses to recognise or negotiate with any union for cabin crew.\n</p><p>In 2011, a former Ryanair captain was awarded financial compensation by an employment tribunal in London after being fired for handing out a union form to a cabin crew member while on duty.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Ryanair_Pilot_Group" title="Ryanair Pilot Group">Ryanair Pilot Group</a> (RPG) was formed, but to date has not been successful in its aim to represent the pilots flying for Ryanair as a collective bargaining unit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Thousands of flights cancellations on 15 September 2017 triggered pilots to mobilise and on 15 December, in Italy, Ireland and Portugal, O\xe2\x80\x98Leary recognized unions for the first time, blaming their good timing; he anticipated an uptick in <a href="/wiki/Labor_cost" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor cost">labor costs</a> in 2018, not altering its model.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\nRyanair discussed union recognition in response to threatened strikes over the Christmas period.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment_conditions">Employment conditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Employment conditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Ryanair faced criticism for allegedly forcing pilots to pay tens of thousands of euros for training, then establish <a href="/wiki/Limited_company" title="Limited company">limited companies</a> in Ireland to have the pilots work for Ryanair through an agency,<sup id="cite_ref-Employee1_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Employee1-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> as well as forcing ground staff in Spain to open bank accounts in <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> in which to receive their wages.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2014, Ryanair\'s office in Marseille was raided by French police investigating complaints that the company was failing to follow French employment law. Ryanair protested about the raid.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2015, the Mayor of Copenhagen announced a boycott of Ryanair. This came in the wake of protests from Danish unions regarding employment conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Employee2_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Employee2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After a court trial confirmed the unions\' right to <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">strike</a>, Ryanair moved its bases out of Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 August 2018, pilots of Ryanair in Germany, Sweden, Ireland, Belgium and the Netherlands walked out for 24 hours, leaving 400 flights cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-Employee3_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Employee3-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> It is considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (November 2018)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to be one of the biggest strikes over pay issues.\n</p><p>On 26 September 2018, Ryanair was forced to cancel 150 flights scheduled for that day, accounting for roughly 6% of its total flights, due to strikes in Spain, Belgium, the Netherlands, Portugal, Italy, and Germany. The British <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> (CAA) urged the company to compensate the 2,400 affected passengers under <a href="/wiki/Flight_Compensation_Regulation_261/2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight Compensation Regulation 261/2004">EU Regulation 261</a>, but Ryanair stated it would refuse to accept any claims for compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In December 2018, the Civil Aviation Authority announced that it would be taking legal action against Ryanair over its refusal to compensate thousands of UK-based customers.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancillary_revenue_and_in-flight_service">Ancillary revenue and in-flight service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ancillary revenue and in-flight service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Twenty percent of Ryanair\'s revenue is generated from <a href="/wiki/Ancillary_revenue" title="Ancillary revenue">ancillary revenue</a>; that is, income from sources other than ticket fares. In 2009, ancillary revenue was at \xe2\x82\xac598&#160;million, compared to a total revenue of \xe2\x82\xac2,942&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ryanair has been described by the consumer magazine <i>Holiday Which?</i> as being the worst offender for charging for optional extras.<sup id="cite_ref-Charges1_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charges1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> As part of the low-cost business model, the airline charges fees, which can be related to alternative services such as using airport check-in facilities instead of the online service fee and paying by credit card. It also charges for extra services like checked-in luggage and it offers food and drinks for purchase as part of a <a href="/wiki/Buy_on_board" title="Buy on board">buy on board</a> programme.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009, Ryanair abolished airport check-in and replaced it with a fast bag drop for those passengers checking in bags.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The option of checking in at the airport for \xe2\x82\xac10 has been discontinued, and all passengers are required to check-in online and print their own boarding pass. Passengers arriving at the airport without a pre-printed online check-in will have to pay \xe2\x82\xac55/\xc2\xa345 for their boarding pass to be re-issued, whilst customers unable to check-in luggage online are asked to pay a fee which varies depending on where they are traveling to at the airport (as of June 2012). Ryanair faced criticism over the ambiguous nature of these changes.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Charges2_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charges2-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="No-frills">No-frills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: No-frills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>New Ryanair aircraft have been delivered with non-reclining seats, no seat-back pockets, safety cards stuck on the back of the seats, and life jackets stowed overhead rather than under the seat. This allows the airline to save on aircraft costs and enables faster cleaning and security checks during the short turnaround times.<sup id="cite_ref-cutfrills_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cutfrills-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> It was reported in various media platforms that Ryanair wanted to order its aircraft without window shades,<sup id="cite_ref-cutfrills_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cutfrills-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> but the new aircraft do have them, as it is required by the regulations of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Aviation_Authority" title="Irish Aviation Authority">Irish Aviation Authority</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Other proposed measures to reduce frills further have included eliminating two toilets to add six more seats,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> redesigning the aircraft to allow <a href="/wiki/Standing_passenger" title="Standing passenger">standing passengers</a> travelling in "<a href="/wiki/Vertical_seat" title="Vertical seat">vertical seats</a>", charging passengers for using the toilet,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> charging extra for overweight passengers,<sup id="cite_ref-Charges3_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charges3-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> and asking passengers to carry their checked-in luggage to the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> While CEO <a href="/wiki/Michael_O%27Leary_(businessman)" title="Michael O&#39;Leary (businessman)">Michael O\'Leary</a> initially claimed that charging passengers for toilets was "going to happen", he stated days later that it was "technically impossible and legally difficult" but "[made] for interesting and very cheap PR".<sup id="cite_ref-Stunt1_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stunt1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Customer_service">Customer service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Customer service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Ryanair has been criticised for many aspects of its customer service. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> wrote that Ryanair\'s "cavalier treatment of passengers" had given Ryanair "a deserved reputation for nastiness" and that the airline "has become a byword for appalling customer service&#160;... and jeering rudeness towards anyone or anything that gets in its way".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In January 2019, a survey conducted by <i>Which?</i> found that the airline was the UK\'s least-liked short-haul airline, for the sixth year running.<sup id="cite_ref-Which1_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Which1-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair responded by saying that passenger numbers had risen 80% in the previous six years and this was a more accurate reflection of the airline\'s popularity than an "unrepresentative survey of just 8,000 people."<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_popularity_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_popularity-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In August 2019, Ryanair came bottom in an annual <i>Which?</i> survey rating the customer services of 100 popular UK brands.<sup id="cite_ref-Which2_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Which2-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002, the High Court in Dublin awarded Jane O\'Keefe \xe2\x82\xac67,500 damages and her costs after Ryanair reneged on a free travel prize she was awarded for being the airline\'s 1 millionth passenger.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airline has come under heavy criticism for its poor treatment of disabled passengers. In 2002, it refused to provide <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair" title="Wheelchair">wheelchairs</a> for disabled passengers at London Stansted Airport, greatly angering disabled rights groups.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The airline argued that this provision was the responsibility of the airport authority, stating that wheelchairs were provided by 80 of the 84 Ryanair destination airports,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> at that time. A court ruling in 2004 judged that the responsibility should be shared by the airline and the airport owners;<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair responded by adding a surcharge of \xc2\xa30.50 to all its flight prices.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph-31012004_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-31012004-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> In July 2012, a 69-year-old woman, Frances Duff, who has a <a href="/wiki/Colostomy" title="Colostomy">colostomy</a>, was refused permission to bring her medical kit on board, despite having a letter from her doctor explaining the need for her to carry this with her, and was asked by Ryanair boarding staff to lift up her shirt in front of fellow passengers, to prove that she had a colostomy bag. Duff had previously attempted to contact Ryanair on three occasions to inquire about its policy regarding travellers\' colostomy bags, but each time no one had answered the phone after half an hour.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> On 4 April 2011, Ryanair began adding a surcharge of \xe2\x82\xac2 to its flights to cover the costs arising from compliance with EC <a href="/wiki/Regulation_261/2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Regulation 261/2004">Regulation 261/2004</a>, which requires it to pay for meals and accommodation for passengers on delayed and cancelled flights.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ryanair did not offer customers the possibility of contacting it by email or <a href="/wiki/Form_(web)" class="mw-redirect" title="Form (web)">webform</a>, only through a premium rate phone line, by fax or by post; however, it does now have a web form contact option. An <a href="/wiki/Early_day_motion" title="Early day motion">early day motion</a> in the British Parliament put forward in 2006 criticised Ryanair for this reason and called on the company to provide customers with a means to contact the company by email.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair offers a basic rate telephone number for post-booking enquiries in the United Kingdom, which chose to omit the exemption for passenger transport services when enacting Article 21 of <a href="/wiki/EU_Consumer_Rights_Directive" class="mw-redirect" title="EU Consumer Rights Directive">Directive 2011/83/EU on Consumer Rights</a> under Regulation 41 of the <i>Consumer Contracts (Information, Cancellation and Additional Payments) Regulations 2013</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Improved_customer_service_and_attracting_families">Improved customer service and attracting families</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Improved customer service and attracting families">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 17 June 2014, Ryanair announced a new campaign to re-invent itself as a more <a href="/wiki/Family-friendly" title="Family-friendly">family-friendly</a> airline. Speaking at the company\'s 2014 AGM, chief executive Michael O\'Leary said that the airline needed to "stop unnecessarily pissing people off". Ryanair said up to 20% of its 81 million customers were travelling as families, and it wanted to raise that figure. Kenny Jacobs, Ryanair\'s chief marketing officer, said: "Families are a big deal for us. It\'s a group of customers that we want to get closer to".<sup id="cite_ref-Ryanair_Woos_Families_in_Bid_To_Shed_More_Abrasive_Image._152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ryanair_Woos_Families_in_Bid_To_Shed_More_Abrasive_Image.-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> As another step, the company launched <a href="/wiki/LiveChat" title="LiveChat">LiveChat</a> on its website to improve the quality of service and experience provided by the company.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> This change in their approach had an almost immediate positive effect on company\'s finances.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_cancellations_September_and_October_2017">Flight cancellations September and October 2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Flight cancellations September and October 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Ryanair was subject to widespread criticism<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent.ie_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.ie-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Independent_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> after it announced that it would be cancelling between 40 and 50 flights per day (about 2% of total daily flights) during September and October 2017. Flights were cancelled with very little notice, sometimes only hours before departure. People who had already taken outbound flights were left with no flight home. Ryanair said that the cancellations aimed "to improve its system-wide punctuality"<sup id="cite_ref-Cancellations_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cancellations-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> which had dropped significantly in the first two weeks of September, which the airline attributed to "ATC capacity delays and strikes, weather disruptions and the impact of increased holiday allocations to pilots and cabin crew".<sup id="cite_ref-Cancellations_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cancellations-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In subsequent statements, Ryanair acknowledged that it had "messed up" holiday schedules for pilots, including a change to the calendar year for how vacations were calculated.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late December, a survey rated Ryanair and <a href="/wiki/Vueling" title="Vueling">Vueling</a> equally the worst in the world for customer service among short-haul carriers in the <i>Which?</i> survey. Ryanair responded, "[t]his survey of 9,000 <i>Which?</i> members is unrepresentative and worthless, during a year when Ryanair is the world\xe2\x80\x99s largest international airline (129m customers) and is also the world\xe2\x80\x99s fastest-growing airline (up to 9m customers in 2017). We have apologised for the deeply regretted flight cancellations and winter schedule changes, and the disruption they caused to less than 1% of our customers".<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publicity">Publicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Publicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="CO2_emissions">CO<sub>2</sub> emissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: CO2 emissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2018, Ryanair became the first airline and the only non-<a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_power_station" title="Fossil fuel power station">coal-power plant</a> to be among the 10 companies with the highest amount of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth&#39;s atmosphere">CO<sub>2</sub>  emissions</a> in the EU. That year, Ryanair had an emission equivalent of 9.9 megatonnes of CO<sub>2</sub> . Emissions had risen by 49% over the course of five years. Environmentalists criticized the airline harshly and saw it as a sign for the lack of taxation of aviation.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, Ryanair was criticised for releasing <a href="/wiki/Ryanair#Misleading_advertising" title="Ryanair">misleading advertisements</a> through their claim they were "Europe\'s\xe2\x80\xa6 Lowest Emissions Airline", using figures from an airline efficiency rating dating back to 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversial_advertising">Controversial advertising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Controversial advertising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg/220px-EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg/330px-EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg/440px-EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="716" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EI-DLM_with_%22Bye_Bye_Latehansa%22_slogan_at_Gerona_Costa_Brava_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Ryanair <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a> displaying <i>"bye bye Latehansa"</i> titles referring to German competitor <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> in 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>Ryanair\'s advertising and the antics of Michael O\'Leary, such as deliberately courting controversy to generate free publicity for the airline,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> have led to a number of complaints to the <a href="/wiki/Advertising_Standards_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Advertising Standards Authority (United Kingdom)">Advertising Standards Authority</a> (ASA) and occasionally court action being taken against the airline.<sup id="cite_ref-brandchannel.com_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brandchannel.com-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stunt2_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stunt2-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An example of this was the live BBC News interview on 27 February 2009 when Michael O\'Leary, observing that it was "a quiet news day", commented that Ryanair was considering charging passengers \xc2\xa31 to use the toilet on its flights. The story subsequently made headlines in the media for several days and drew attention to Ryanair\'s announcement that it was removing check-in desks from airports and replacing them with online check-in. Eight days later O\'Leary eventually admitted that it was a publicity stunt saying "It is not likely to happen, but it makes for interesting and very cheap PR".<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The concept of Ryanair charging for even this most essential of customer services was foreseen by the spoof news website "The Mardale Times" some five months previously, in its article "Ryanair announce new \'Pay-Per-Poo\' service".<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ryanair often uses advertising to make direct comparisons and attack its competitors. One of its advertisements used a picture of the <i><a href="/wiki/Manneken_Pis" title="Manneken Pis">Manneken Pis</a></i>, a famous Belgian statue of a urinating child, with the words: "Pissed off with <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a>\'s high fares? Low fares have arrived in Belgium." Sabena sued and the court ruled that the advertisements were misleading and offensive. Ryanair was ordered to discontinue the advertisements immediately or face fines. Ryanair was also obliged to publish an apology and publish the court decision on its website. Ryanair used the apologies for further advertising, primarily for further price comparisons.<sup id="cite_ref-brandchannel.com_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brandchannel.com-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another provocative ad campaign headlined "Expensive <i>BA</i>stards!" compared Ryanair with <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>. As with Sabena, British Airways disagreed with the accompanying price comparisons and brought legal action against Ryanair. However, in this case, the High Court sided with Ryanair and threw BA\'s case out ordering the BA to make a payment towards Ryanair\'s court costs. The judge ruled "The complaint amounts to this: that Ryanair exaggerated in suggesting BA is five times more expensive because BA is only three times more expensive."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, Ryanair used an advertisement for its new <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> route which showed <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a> (<a href="/wiki/First_Minister_and_deputy_First_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="First Minister and deputy First Minister">Northern Ireland deputy First Minister</a> and a former senior commander of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">IRA</a>) standing alongside party president <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Adams" title="Gerry Adams">Gerry Adams</a> with a speech bubble which said "Ryanair fares are so low even the British Army flew home".<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Ulster Unionists reacted angrily to the advertisement, while the Advertising Standards Authority said it did not believe the ad would cause widespread offence.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An advertisement depicting a model dressed as a schoolgirl was accompanied by the words "Hottest back to school fares". Ryanair ran the advertisement in two Scottish and one UK-wide newspaper. After receiving 13 complaints, the advertisement was widely reported by national newspapers. The Advertising Standards Authority (ASA) instructed the airline to withdraw the advertisement in the United Kingdom, saying that it "appeared to link teenage girls with sexually provocative behaviour and was irresponsible and likely to cause serious or widespread offence". Ryanair said that it would "not be withdrawing this ad" and would "not provide the ASA with any of the undertakings they seek", on the basis that it found it absurd that "a picture of a fully clothed model is now claimed to cause \'serious or widespread offence\', when many of the UK\'s leading daily newspapers regularly run pictures of topless or partially dressed females without causing any serious or widespread offence".<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2020, the airline faced criticism over its \xe2\x80\x9cjab and go\xe2\x80\x9d advert.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Misleading_advertising">Misleading advertising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Misleading advertising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Although it usually does not serve the primary airports of major European cities, Ryanair has been criticised for placing the names of famous cities on distant secondary airports that were not built for tourist traffic and lacked transit links to the main city. Examples include "<a href="/wiki/Beauvais%E2%80%93Till%C3%A9_Airport" title="Beauvais\xe2\x80\x93Till\xc3\xa9 Airport">Paris Beauvais</a>" (85&#160;km (53&#160;mi) north-northwest of Paris), "<a href="/wiki/Brussels_South_Charleroi_Airport" title="Brussels South Charleroi Airport">Brussels South</a>" (46&#160;km (29&#160;mi) to the south of Brussels), "<a href="/wiki/Orio_al_Serio_International_Airport" title="Orio al Serio International Airport">Milan Bergamo</a>" (45&#160;km (28&#160;mi) from Milan), "<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt%E2%80%93Hahn_Airport" title="Frankfurt\xe2\x80\x93Hahn Airport">Frankfurt Hahn</a>" (102&#160;km (63&#160;mi) from Frankfurt and actually closer to the cities of <a href="/wiki/Koblenz" title="Koblenz">Koblenz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Weeze_Airport" title="Weeze Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Weeze</a>" (83&#160;km (52&#160;mi) from D\xc3\xbcsseldorf), "<a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Skavsta_Airport" title="Stockholm Skavsta Airport">Stockholm Skavsta</a>" (89&#160;km (55&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>), and "<a href="/wiki/Reus_Airport" title="Reus Airport">Barcelona Reus</a>" (88&#160;km (55&#160;mi) from Barcelona). <i>Frommers</i> has dubbed Ryanair the "ultimate <a href="/wiki/Bait-and-switch" title="Bait-and-switch">bait-and-switch</a> airline" for this deceptive practice.<sup id="cite_ref-frommers3_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frommers3-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ryanair was ordered by the ASA to stop claiming that its flights from London to Brussels were faster than the rail connection <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a>, on the grounds that the claim was misleading, due to required travel times to the airports mentioned. Ryanair stood by its claims, noting that the flight time is shorter than the train trip and that travel time is also required to reach Eurostar\'s stations.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2008, Ryanair faced a probe by the UK <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Trading" title="Office of Fair Trading">Office of Fair Trading</a>, after a string of complaints about its adverts. It was found to have breached advertising rules seven times in two years. ASA\'s director general Christopher Graham commented that formal referrals to the OFT were rare, the last occurring in 2005. He added that the ASA "would prefer to work with advertisers within the self-regulatory system rather than call in a statutory body, but Ryanair\'s approach has left us with no option". Ryanair countered with the claim that the ASA had "demonstrated a repeated lack of independence, impartiality and fairness".<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2009, Ryanair took a number of steps to "increase the clarity and transparency of its website and other advertising" after reaching an agreement with the OFT. The airline\'s website now includes a statement that "fares don\'t include optional fees/charges" and they now include a table of fees to make fare comparisons easier.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2010, Ryanair once again found itself in controversy regarding alleged misleading advertising. Ryanair circulated advertisements in two newspapers offering \xc2\xa310 one-way fares to European destinations. Following a complaint from rival carrier EasyJet, the ASA ruled the offer was "likely to mislead".<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair made no comment on the claim but did hit back at EasyJet, claiming it cared about details in this regard but did not itself publicise its on-time statistics. EasyJet denied this.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In April 2011, Ryanair advertised \'a place in the sun destinations\' but the advert was banned when it was found that some of the destinations experienced sunshine for as little as three hours per day and temperatures between 0 and 14&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32 and 57&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, Ryanair stated that websites such as <a href="/wiki/Opodo" title="Opodo">Opodo</a> and CheapOair; and their partners; engaged in <a href="/wiki/Data_scraping#Screen_scraping" title="Data scraping">screenscraping</a> and false advertising, and attempted to prevent them from showing Ryanair data.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2020 the <a href="/wiki/Advertising_Standards_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Advertising Standards Authority (United Kingdom)">Advertising Standards Authority</a> told Ryanair to provide adequate evidence to support environmental claims after the ASA banned adverts that claimed Ryanair was the lowest emissions airline in Europe for being misleading.<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair had claimed in the adverts that they had "the lowest carbon emissions of any major airline" and it was a "low CO2 emissions airline" based on Europes top 27 airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The ASA queried some figures and the definition of a "major airline" for the purposes of assessing .<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Complainants said the adverts were misleading and could not be substantiated.<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>  In response to the ASA Ryanair cited data from <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a> and airline efficiency rankings from Brighter Plant.<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> However the ASA said that Ryanair had used an efficiency ranking from 2011 which was "of little value as substantiation for a comparison made in 2019".<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The ASA said that customers would interpret the adverts as saying that flying with Ryanair would mean they contributed fewer <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth&#39;s atmosphere">CO2 emissions</a> to the earth atmosphere, which could not be proven.<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The ASA said that the adverts "ads must not appear again in their current forms" as claims in them could not be substantiated.<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading_186-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-ryanair-lowest-emissions-airline-ad-misleading-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_surcharges">Criticism of surcharges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Criticism of surcharges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In February 2011, a Ryanair passenger, Miro Garcia, brought a claim against Ryanair for unfair surcharges, claiming that the \xe2\x82\xac40 (\xc2\xa330) surcharge on passengers who failed to print out a boarding card prior to arrival at the airport was unfair. Judge Barbara Cordoba, sitting in the Commercial Court in Barcelona, held that, under international air travel conventions, Ryanair can neither demand passengers turn up at the airport with their boarding pass, nor charge them \xe2\x82\xac40 (\xc2\xa330) if they do not, and that the fines were abusive because aviation law obliges airlines to issue boarding passes. Judge Cordoba stated that: "I declare abusive and, therefore, null, the clause in the contract by which Ryanair obliges the passenger to take a boarding pass to the airport... the customary practice over the years has been that the obligation to provide the boarding pass has always fallen on the airline". The judge ordered a refund for Mr. Garcia and said the fact the company was a low-cost carrier did "not allow it to alter its basic contractual obligations".<sup id="cite_ref-Charges4_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charges4-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair appealed the decision and the Appeals Court in Spain overturned the ruling in November 2011, holding that the surcharge is in compliance with international law.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2011, Ryanair announced that it would fight against the UK Treasury\'s plan to ban what <i><a href="/wiki/Which%3F" title="Which?">Which?</a></i> magazine called "rip-off" charges made when customers paid by credit card.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> EU legislation has already been drafted against surcharges for methods of payment.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_incidents">Fuel incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Fuel incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 26 July 2012 three Ryanair aircraft inbound to <a href="/wiki/Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas Airport">Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas Airport</a> diverted to <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Airport" title="Valencia Airport">Valencia Airport</a> due to severe thunderstorms in the Madrid area. All three aircraft declared an emergency (<a href="/wiki/Mayday" title="Mayday">Mayday</a>) when the calculated usable fuel on landing at Valencia Airport was less than final reserve (30 minutes of flight) after having been held in the air for 50 to 69 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The Irish Aviation Authority investigated the incidents and came to a number of conclusions, including:\n</p>\n<ol><li><i>"The aircraft in all three cases departed for Madrid with fuel in excess of Flight Plan requirements"</i>;</li>\n<li><i>"The Crew diverted to Valencia with fuel in excess of the minimum diversion fuel depicted on the Flight Plan"</i>;</li>\n<li><i>"Diverting with fuel close to minimum diversion fuel in the circumstances presented on the evening in question was likely to present challenges for the crew. Initial holding was to the Southwest of Madrid which increased the diversion time to the alternate"</i>;</li>\n<li><i>"The Crew declared an Emergency in accordance with EU-OPS when the calculated usable fuel for landing at Valencia was less than final reserve"</i>;</li>\n<li><i>"The Met conditions in Madrid were more significant than anticipated by the Crew when reviewing the Met Forecast. Consequently, the additional fuel carried was influenced by the forecast"</i>;</li>\n<li><i>"Operations into a busy airport such as Madrid in Thunderstorm conditions with the associated traffic levels can add significant delays to all traffic"</i>;</li>\n<li><i>"Air Traffic Control in Valencia was under significant pressure with the number of diversions arriving in their airspace."</i><sup id="cite_ref-ryanair3_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ryanair3-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>The Irish Aviation Authority made a number of recommendations, including that Ryanair should <i>"review [its] fuel policy and consider issuing guidance to Crew with respect to fuel when operating into busy airports with mixed aircraft operators and types particularly in poor weather conditions when diversions are likely."</i><sup id="cite_ref-ryanair3_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ryanair3-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> The IAA also recommended that the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Aviation_Safety_and_Security_Agency" title="Spanish Aviation Safety and Security Agency">Spanish Aviation Safety and Security Agency</a> <i>"review delays into Madrid to consider if additional fuel should be recommended or required to be carried in normal operations particularly where the southerly Runways are in operation."</i><sup id="cite_ref-ryanair3_191-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ryanair3-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Among the causes of the incident, the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Accident_and_Incident_Investigation_Commission" title="Civil Aviation Accident and Incident Investigation Commission">Civil Aviation Accident and Incident Investigation Commission</a> concluded that <i>"the company\'s fuel savings policy, though it complies with the minimum legal requirements, tends to minimise the amount of fuel with which its aircraft operate and leaves none for contingencies below the legal minimums. This contributed to the amount of fuel used being improperly planned and to the amount of fuel onboard dropping below the required final fuel reserve."</i><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an interview with the Dutch investigative journalism programme <i>KRO Reporter</i>, four anonymous Ryanair pilots claimed they were being pressured to carry as little fuel as possible on board to cut costs.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair and its CEO Michael O\'Leary denied the allegations and sued KRO.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> On 16 April 2014, the Dutch Court decided that <a href="/wiki/Katholieke_Radio_Omroep" title="Katholieke Radio Omroep">KRO</a> had provided sufficient evidence in two television episodes of <i>Mayday, Mayday</i> broadcast in 2012 and 2013 to back the claims in respect of Ryanair\'s fuel policy and "fear culture". It also found that Ryanair had been given a right of reply in response to the claims. The broadcast of the programmes was found to be in the public interest. Ryanair was ordered to pay the legal costs of the case.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurocockpit_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurocockpit-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Handling_of_the_2020_COVID-19_pandemic">Handling of the 2020 COVID-19 pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Handling of the 2020 COVID-19 pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Starting in late March 2020, in response to necessary flight cancellations due to travel restrictions set by governments due to <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a>, Ryanair was forced to cancel flights. This resulted in many of their staff being placed on furlough, with pay being cut by up to 50% for some employees placed on the Irish Temporary Wage Subsidy Scheme (TWSS).<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Travellers with flights cancelled are being offered vouchers or an alternative flight date. Ryanair has said they will not be issuing cash refunds until after the COVID-19 crisis is over, which has angered many customers having to wait months for a refund covered under EU regulations.\n</p><p>The handling of refunds from Ryanair has caused a surge in complaints to the Commission for Aviation Regulation (CAR), with customers claiming that they have been refused a refund for the flight cancellation.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Many organisations have taken a stance against the aviation industry via actions or declarations in the press.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The Italian civil aviation authority <a href="/wiki/Italian_Civil_Aviation_Authority" title="Italian Civil Aviation Authority">ENAC</a> has threatened a ban of Ryanair due to alleged violation of local COVID-19 regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ryanair chief executive Michael O\xe2\x80\x99Leary said its planes would not fly if the airline was required to leave its middle seats empty to comply with in-flight social distancing rules. He said blocking the space between seats was "idiotic" and would have no beneficial effect.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitors">Competitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Competitors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Ryanair has several <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_low-cost_airlines#Europe" title="List of low-cost airlines">competitors</a>. In 2004, approximately 60 new low-cost airlines were formed. Although traditionally a full-service airline, Aer Lingus moved to a low-fares strategy from 2002, leading to a much more intense competition with Ryanair on Irish routes.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair is a member of <a href="/wiki/Airlines_for_Europe" title="Airlines for Europe">Airlines for Europe</a>, having formerly been a member of the defunct <a href="/wiki/European_Low_Fares_Airline_Association" title="European Low Fares Airline Association">European Low Fares Airline Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airlines that attempt to compete directly with Ryanair are treated competitively, with Ryanair being accused by some of reducing fares to significantly undercut its competitors. In response to MyTravelLite, which started to compete with Ryanair on the Birmingham to Dublin route in 2003, Ryanair set up competing flights on some of MyTravelLite\'s routes until it pulled out. <a href="/wiki/Go_Fly" class="mw-redirect" title="Go Fly">Go</a> was another airline that attempted to offer services from Ryanair\'s base at Dublin to Glasgow and Edinburgh in Scotland. A fierce battle ensued, which ended with Go withdrawing its service from Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2004, Ryanair\'s biggest competitor, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, announced routes to the Republic of Ireland for the first time, beginning with the Cork to London Gatwick route. Until then, EasyJet had never competed directly with Ryanair on its home ground. EasyJet later withdrew its Gatwick-Cork, Gatwick-Shannon, Gatwick-Knock and Luton-Shannon routes.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, Ryanair also responded to the decision of another low-cost carrier, <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> that planned to move its flight operations from <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport">Warsaw Chopin Airport</a> in Poland to the new low-cost <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Modlin_Airport" title="Warsaw Modlin Airport">Warsaw Modlin Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nowy_Dw%C3%B3r_Mazowiecki" title="Nowy Dw\xc3\xb3r Mazowiecki">Nowy Dw\xc3\xb3r Mazowiecki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair had previously operated the route to Dublin from Warsaw but withdrew, claiming that the fees at Warsaw\'s main airport were too high. When Wizz Air began operations from Modlin Airport, Ryanair began several new routes from the same airport, most of which were identical to routes offered by Wizz Air.\n</p><p>In 2008, Ryanair asked the Irish high court to investigate why it had been refused permission to fly from <a href="/wiki/Ireland_West_Airport_Knock" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland West Airport Knock">Knock</a> to Dublin. This route was won by CityJet, which was unable to operate the service. The runner up, <a href="/wiki/Aer_Arann" class="mw-redirect" title="Aer Arann">Aer Arann</a>, was then allowed to start flights, a move Ryanair criticises on the basis of not initiating an additional tender process was unlawful.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/DFDS" title="DFDS">DFDS Seaways</a> cited competition from low-cost air services, especially Ryanair, which now flies to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh Airport</a> and London Stansted Airport from <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_Landvetter_Airport" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg Landvetter Airport">Gothenburg Landvetter Airport</a>, as the reason for scrapping the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a> ferry service in October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> It was the only dedicated passenger ferry service between Sweden and the United Kingdom and had been running under various operators since the 19th century.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ryanair_destinations" title="List of Ryanair destinations">List of Ryanair destinations</a></div>\n<p>Ryanair\'s largest base is at <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">London-Stansted</a> with 44 aircraft followed by its home base at Dublin Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair operates from 84 bases connecting 35 countries across Europe and North Africa, some of which only base a single aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Several non-base airports serve more flights and/or destinations than certain base airports.\n</p><p>Ryanair traditionally prefers to fly to smaller or secondary airports usually outside major cities to help the company benefit from lower landing fees and quick turn-around times to reduce costs. Ryanair has even referred to <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_Airport" title="Bratislava Airport">Bratislava Airport</a> in Slovakia as "Bratislava Vienna", despite Vienna being 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) away and across a national border. In some cases, secondary airports are not distant from the city they serve, and can in fact can be closer than the city\'s major airport; this is the case at <a href="/wiki/Rome_Ciampino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Ciampino Airport">Rome Ciampino Airport</a>.\n</p><p>Ryanair does still serve a number of major airports, including <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport" title="Athens International Airport">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_El_Prat_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Barcelona El Prat Airport">Barcelona El Prat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels Zaventem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport" title="Budapest Ferenc Liszt International Airport">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Portela_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Portela Airport">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">London-Gatwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Barajas_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrid Barajas Airport">Madrid Barajas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marseille_Provence_Airport" title="Marseille Provence Airport">Marseille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen" title="Oslo Airport, Gardermoen">Oslo-Gardermoen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rome_Fiumicino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Fiumicino Airport">Rome-Fiumicino</a>. Some of these cities do not have a viable secondary airport that Ryanair could use as an alternative.<sup id="cite_ref-frommers3_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frommers3-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In more recent months/years, Ryanair has grown more at primary airports as it looks to attract more business passengers. For summer 2014, the airline opened bases in Athens, Lisbon and the primary airports of Brussels and Rome for the first time.\n</p><p>Ryanair flies in a <a href="/wiki/Point-to-point_transit" title="Point-to-point transit">point to point model</a> rather than the more traditional airline <a href="/wiki/Spoke-hub_distribution_paradigm" class="mw-redirect" title="Spoke-hub distribution paradigm">hub and spoke</a> model where the passengers have to change aircraft in transit at a major airport, usually being able to reach more destinations this way.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> In April 2017 Ryanair added more indirect flights to its portfolio, starting with a new transfer hub in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>-Fiumicino airport (FCO).<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair has 50 European bases. Despite it being an Irish airline, and having a significant presence there, it also has a significant presence in France, Germany, Italy, Poland, Spain, the United Kingdom as well as many other European countries. Currently, its biggest country market is Italy, with fourteen bases and nine non-base airports.\n</p><p>Ryanair\'s largest competitor is EasyJet which has a far greater focus on larger or primary airports such as <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Schiphol Airport">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris-Charles de Gaulle</a>, heavily targeting business passengers. Ryanair also serves sun and beach destinations with bases in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Islands">Greek Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> among others. In August 2014, the airline unveiled ambitious plans to establish a major hub in Israel to service a broad range of European routes.<sup id="cite_ref-RyanairIsrael_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RyanairIsrael-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> In December 2014 Ryanair announced plans to open its 72nd base in 2015 in the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018, due to the Scottish Government not abolishing or reducing Air Passenger Duty (APD), Ryanair announced that it would cut many flights out of <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow Airport</a> resulting in the airline closing its base there. The only routes out of Glasgow by the end of October were Dublin, Krak\xc3\xb3w and Wroclaw, with the rest being suspended permanently. This resulted in the loss of 300 members of airport staff. In April 2019, the airline reinstated four of its routes; to Alicante, Brussels, M\xc3\xa1laga and Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n<caption>Top airports by destinations<br />(only 48+ destinations)<br />November class="mw-headline" id="Choosing_destinations">Choosing destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Choosing destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When Ryanair negotiates with airport operators, it demands very low landing and handling fees, as well as financial assistance with marketing and promotional campaigns.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> In subsequent contract renewal negotiations, the airline has been reported to play airports against each other, threatening to withdraw services and deploy the aircraft elsewhere, if the airport does not make further concessions. According to Michael O\'Leary\'s biography, <i>A Life in Full Flight</i>, Ryanair\'s growing popularity and also growing bargaining power, with both airports and aircraft manufacturers, has resulted in the airline being less concerned about a market research/demographics approach to route selection to one based more on experimentation. This means it is more likely to fly its aircraft between the lowest cost airports in anticipation that its presence alone on that route will be sufficient to create a demand which previously may not have existed, either in whole or in part.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2006, a failure to reach agreement on a new commercial contract resulted in Ryanair announcing that it would withdraw service on the Dublin\xe2\x80\x93Cardiff route at short notice.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> The airport management rebutted Ryanair\'s assertion that airport charges were unreasonably high, claiming that the Cardiff charges were already below Ryanair\'s average and claimed that Ryanair had recently adopted the same negotiating approach with <a href="/wiki/Cork_Airport" title="Cork Airport">Cork Airport</a> and London Stansted Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Ryanair was reported to have adopted \'harsh\' negotiating with <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon Airport</a>, threatening to close 75% of its operations there from April 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-rte.ie_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte.ie-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair was forced to give up its <a href="/wiki/Rome_Ciampino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Ciampino Airport">Rome Ciampino</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Alghero" title="Alghero">Alghero</a> route, after the route was allocated to <a href="/wiki/Air_One" title="Air One">Air One</a>, as a <a href="/wiki/Public_service_obligation" title="Public service obligation">public service obligation</a> (PSO) route. The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> is investigating the actions of the Italian Government in assigning PSO routes and thus restricting competition. In 2016 Ryanair withdrew over half of its flights from <a href="/wiki/Moss_Airport,_Rygge" title="Moss Airport, Rygge">Rygge airport</a> in Norway, after which the airport decided to close down totally, as they were privately owned and would make a loss on the low traffic volume.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Fleet">edit</a><span title="Boeing 737 800">Boeing 737-800</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_group_fleet">Current group fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span livery.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_fleet">Former fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Former fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Ryanair has operated the following types of aircraft in the past:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="border-collapse:collapse;text-align:center">\n<caption>Ryanair past fleet\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Aircraft\n</th>\n<th>Introduced\n</th>\n<th>Retired\n</th>\n<th>Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/ATR_42-300" class="mw-redirect" title="ATR 42-300">ATR 42-300</a><sup id="cite_ref-airfleetsnethistory_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airfleetsnethistory-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>1989\n</td>\n<td>1991\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven 500</a><sup id="cite_ref-ab_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ab-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>1986\n</td>\n<td>1994\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="#cite_note-airfleetsnethistory-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>1994\n</td>\n<td>2005\n</td>\n<td>Replaced by 737-800. Ryanair sold its fleet of 20 737-200 aircraft to Autodirect Aviation LLC for $8.1 million in October 2004.<br />6 Aircraft had already been retired and the remaining 14 were transferred between 2004-2005.<sup id="cite_ref-200_sale_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200_sale-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-300">Boeing 737-300</a><sup id="cite_ref-airfleetsnethistory_229-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airfleetsnethistory-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>2002\n</td>\n<td>2004\n</td>\n<td>Replaced by 737-800\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-400"
