href="#cite_note-airfleetsnethistory-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>2004\n</td>\n<td>2005\n</td>\n<td>Leased from <a href="/wiki/Air_Atlanta_Icelandic" title="Air Atlanta Icelandic">Air Atlanta Icelandic</a> and AirExplore (during Summer 2014<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>).\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Embraer_EMB_110_Bandeirante" title="Embraer EMB 110 Bandeirante">Embraer EMB 110 Bandeirante</a><sup id="cite_ref-ab_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ab-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>1985\n</td>\n<td>1989\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748" title="Hawker Siddeley HS 748">Hawker Siddeley HS 748</a><sup id="cite_ref-ab_230-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ab-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>1986\n</td>\n<td>1990\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet_development">Fleet development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Fleet development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX_groundings" title="Boeing 737 MAX groundings">grounding of all 737 MAX aircraft</a>, Ryanair initially reaffirmed its confidence in the aircraft and indicated that it would be ready to place a new order once it had returned to service; it would seek a reduced price in lieu of cash compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> In July that year, it warned that some of its bases would be subject to short-term closures in 2020, due to the shortfall in MAX deliveries, and pointed out that the MAX 200 version it has ordered will require separate certification expected to take a further two months after the MAX returns to service.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> In the same month, O\'Leary expressed concerns and frustration with the certification delays and revealed that, in parallel with discussions with Boeing regarding a potential order for new aircraft to be delivered from 2023, he was also talking to Airbus which was offering very aggressive pricing.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of March 2018, the average age of the Ryanair fleet was around 6.5 years,<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> roughly 2 years older than some of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> When Boeing builds an aircraft for Ryanair, it is allocated the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Boeing_customer_codes" title="List of Boeing customer codes">customer code</a> AS, which appears in its aircraft designation as an infix, such as 737-8AS.\n</p><p>Ryanair\'s fleet reached 200 aircraft for the first time on 5 September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-ryanair.com_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ryanair.com-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> All aircraft in the Ryanair fleet have been <a href="/wiki/Retrofit" class="mw-redirect" title="Retrofit">retrofitted</a> with performance enhancing <a href="/wiki/Winglets" class="mw-redirect" title="Winglets">winglets</a> and the more recent deliveries have them fitted as standard.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company also owns three <a href="/wiki/Learjet_45" title="Learjet 45">Learjet 45</a> business jets, based at <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">London Stansted Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bergamo_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bergamo Airport">Bergamo Airport</a> but registered in the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, which are mainly used for the quick transportation of maintenance personnel and small aircraft parts around the network.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 March 2013, Ryanair signed an order for 175 new Boeing 737-800s. In the press conference announcing the order, Michael O\'Leary said Ryanair was still evaluating the possibility of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">Boeing 737 MAX</a>, and stated its huge order in March was for the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737 Next Generation</a> rather than the 737 MAX as it needed aircraft before the 737 MAX would enter service.\n</p><p>On 30 April 2014, Ryanair confirmed that it had ordered five more aircraft to add to its fleet, four of them to be delivered in 2015 and the last one to be delivered in February 2016, to bring the number of aircraft on order to 180.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Summer 2014, Ryanair contracted <a href="/wiki/AirExplore" title="AirExplore">AirExplore</a> to operate some of their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.routesonline.com/news/29/breaking-news/240596/ryanair-set-to-lease-737-400s-to-support-dublin-growth/">summer flights</a> between London Stansted and Dublin airport. Four 737-400\'s were supposedly leased as shown from a report by Airport Coordination Limited (ACL). When questioned about the leasing, Ryanair stubbornly refused to state they don\'t "comment upon, or engage in, rumour or speculation." but <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Qv-L6Y1A2BY">footage</a> confirms it occurred. The leasing was done in part due to the route growth potential partly due to the abolition of the Irish \xe2\x82\xac3 travel tax in April 2014 and demand for planes from new routes led to shortages of 737-800\'s.\n</p><p>Ryanair also showed interest in other aircraft, including the <a href="/wiki/Comac_C919" title="Comac C919">Comac C919</a>, when it signed a design agreement with Comac in 2011 to help produce a rival jet to Boeing\'s offerings. At the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Airshow" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Airshow">Paris Airshow</a> in 2013, Michael O\'Leary stated that <a href="/wiki/Comac" title="Comac">Comac</a> could build a larger version of the C919 aircraft that would hold up to 200 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 September 2014, Ryanair made a commitment to order 100 new <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">Boeing 737 MAX 8s</a> (plus options for an additional 100) for delivery from 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-737max_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-737max-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 December 2014, the airline finalised its order for up to 200 Boeing 737 MAX 200s, a version of the 737 MAX 8 for low-cost airlines, named after the fact that they can carry 200 passengers. The order includes 100 firm, and 100 purchase rights. This makes Ryanair the launch customer of the Boeing 737 MAX 200.<sup id="cite_ref-Ryanair_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ryanair-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 10 November 2008, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair_Flight_4102" title="Ryanair Flight 4102">Ryanair Flight 4102</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt%E2%80%93Hahn_Airport" title="Frankfurt\xe2\x80\x93Hahn Airport">Frankfurt\xe2\x80\x93Hahn Airport</a>, suffered undercarriage damage in an emergency landing at <a href="/wiki/Rome%E2%80%93Ciampino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome\xe2\x80\x93Ciampino Airport">Rome\xe2\x80\x93Ciampino Airport</a>, after experiencing <a href="/wiki/Bird_strike" title="Bird strike">bird strikes</a>, which damaged both engines on approach. There were six crew members and 166 passengers on board.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Two crew members and eight passengers were taken to hospital with minor injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Herald_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herald-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> The port undercarriage of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800</a> collapsed,<sup id="cite_ref-Ciampino_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ciampino-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> leaving the aircraft stranded on the runway and closing the airport for over 35 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-Herald_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herald-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> As well as damage to the engines and undercarriage, the rear fuselage was also damaged by contact with the runway.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft involved was damaged beyond repair and was scrapped. The final report of the accident, investigated by <a href="/wiki/Agenzia_Nazionale_per_la_Sicurezza_del_Volo" title="Agenzia Nazionale per la Sicurezza del Volo">ANSV</a> (National Flight Safety Agency) was released on 20 December 2018, more than 10 years after the accident and only in Italian.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> An English translation was provided by Aviation Accident Database.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ryanair&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span
